Maturidi's Argument from Design Against Astrology
Maturidi argues from design against star agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the precise design of the universe to refute the claim that stars are independent agents.

Core Idea
The universe's perfect design points to a wise Maker, not tired stars.

Maturidi begins by critiquing the view that the stars themselves cause events. He points out that the precise and perfect actions we observe can only come from a being with knowledge and power. If stars were intelligent agents, they would be exhausted by perpetual motion; if they are inanimate, they must be directed by another. This sets the stage for his broader refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on design
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi builds his argument from the Maker's perfect action to the analogy with stars.
The passage uses a syllogistic structure: if stars were self-governing, they would tire; they don't tire, so they are not self-governing.
2
Identify the two case scenarios for stars
Maturidi presents two possibilities: stars are alive (like animals) or inanimate. For each, he shows they cannot be independent agents. Find these two cases in the text.
The living case: they would tire. The inanimate case: they must be controlled by another.
3
Reflect on the implication
Think about why Maturidi includes the story of the brocade and the point about the Maker's self-sufficiency. How does this strengthen the design argument?
The brocade shows that a complex product implies a skilled maker, similar to the universe.
4
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question based solely on this passage.
The answer can be found in the lines about stars tiring themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تكلم هؤلاء بما تكلم به أصحاب الطبائع : إن ذلك الصانع إنما خرج فعله محكما متقنا بما عنده من العلم وله من القدرة، ولولا ذلك لما احتمل ما ذكرت؛ فإنه بما سبق من التدبير استقام ذلك؛ فمثله أمر النجوم . لو كان على ما يقول كان يكون ذلك كذلك بتدبير عليم حكيم أنشأها على ذلك. ولو كان إليها التدبير لما يحتمل أن تُتعب نفسها بالسير والحركات الدائمة وتؤلمها ؛ إذ كذلك حال الأحياء في الشاهد: إن تلك الأحوال تتعبهم وتؤلمهم أو أن يكون من الموات فيكون بتدبير غيرها كان الذي كان، على ما ذكر من قصة الديباج. على أنه يُعلم أنه لو قدر على ذلك بلا إتعاب نفسه لاختاره عليه. لِيُعْلَمْ أن كل ذلك بتدبير حكيم عليم غنى استعمل جميع ما ذكر فيما ذكر . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول في عالمنا : إنه بتدبير من ذكر الجاز مثله فيمن ذكر أنه كان بتدبير من يعلوه، كذلك إلى ما لا نهاية له، وفي ذلك بطلان قولهم في تدبير النجوم؛ أو يرجع نهاية، وفي ذلك فساد قولهم في رفع النهاية عن الأشياء وإيجاب القول بواحد إليه يرجع تدبير جميع ما ذكر.
Then these people spoke as the proponents of natures spoke: 'Indeed that Maker only brought forth His action precisely and perfectly because of the knowledge He possesses and the power He has. Were it not for that, what you mentioned would not be possible. For by the prior planning it became sound; similarly is the matter of the stars. If it were as he says, it would be thus by the planning of a wise knowing one who established them upon that. And if planning belonged to them, they would not be able to tire themselves with perpetual motion and movement and cause themselves pain; for such is the condition of living beings in the witnessed world: those states tire and pain them. Or if they were inanimate, then they would be under the planning of another, as occurred in the story of the brocade. Moreover, it is known that if it were capable of that without tiring itself, it would have chosen it over it. So let it be known that all that is by the planning of a wise, knowing, self-sufficient one who employed all that was mentioned for what was mentioned. And there is no power except with God. Then, if it were permissible to say concerning our world that it is under the planning of someone mentioned, then it would be permissible similarly concerning someone mentioned that he was under the planning of one above him, and so on ad infinitum. In that is the invalidation of their claim about the planning of the stars; or it terminates in an end, and in that is the corruption of their claim of removing the end from things and necessitating the assertion of a single one to whom the planning of all that was mentioned returns.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of astrological determinism. Maturidi presents an argument from design: the precise and perfect actions of the Maker show that He has knowledge and power. Similarly, if the stars were intelligent agents, they would be fatigued by perpetual motion, like living beings. If they are inanimate, they must be controlled by another. Maturidi then presents a second argument: if we attribute planning to any entity, we can ask who planned that entity, leading to infinite regress. The only way to stop this regress is to affirm a single ultimate Planner, thereby invalidating the astrologers' claim that stars independently cause events.

Key Terms
الصانع
التدبير
النجوم
الحكيم العليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi denies any causal role for stars whatsoever.
Correction: He denies that stars are independent agents, but they may still be signs or instruments under God's control.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument from design, what would happen if stars were intelligent agents directing their own motion?
A) They would be more efficient.
B) They would be tired from perpetual motion.
C) They would be inanimate.
D) They would be self-sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The universe's design shows that stars cannot be independent planners; only a wise, powerful Maker can account for it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the precise order of the universe—from the stars to your own heartbeat—do you truly see it as the act of a wise Planner, or do you sometimes fall into thinking it is mere coincidence? What would change in your daily gratitude if you constantly reminded yourself that nothing is random?
?
Have you ever felt exhausted by your own efforts, as if you were a star trying to sustain itself by its own motion? How does knowing that the true Planner is self-sufficient and never tires free you from the burden of thinking you must control everything?
?
The brocade analogy shows that a beautiful design requires a weaver. Look at one area of your life where you see disorder or struggle. Can you trust that the wise Planner is at work even there, and commit today to stop trying to be the weaver yourself?

Maturidi's Infinite Regress Argument Against Astrology
Maturidi refutes astrology via infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the impossibility of infinite regress to prove that all planning ultimately goes back to a single Creator, refuting the independent agency of stars.

Core Idea
If stars cause events, who caused the stars? Infinite regress leads to absurdity, so a single Planner is necessary.

After showing that stars cannot be independent agents, Maturidi presents a second argument: if we attribute planning to any entity, we must then ask who planned that entity. This leads either to an infinite chain, which is impossible, or to a single ultimate Planner. This argument effectively refutes the astrological claim that stars are self-sufficient causes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on infinite regress
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical structure: if we allow planning for one entity, we must allow it for its planner, creating a chain.
The phrase 'lo jaza' (if it were permissible) sets up a conditional.
2
Identify the two options
Maturidi presents two outcomes of the chain: infinite regress (invalidation) or termination in an end (which necessitates a single Planner). Find these two options in the text.
The words 'la nihaya' (no end) and 'nihaya' (end) are key.
3
Understand the conclusion
Contemplate why infinite regress is invalid and why affirming an 'end' leads to the assertion of one ultimate Planner. How does this refute the astrologers?
If stars plan, who planned the stars? If that planner is another star, we keep going. Only stopping at God saves the argument.
4
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding with the multiple-choice question.
The answer is directly from the passage about infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then these people spoke as the proponents of natures spoke: 'Indeed that Maker only brought forth His action precisely and perfectly because of the knowledge He possesses and the power He has. Were it not for that, what you mentioned would not be possible. For by the prior planning it became sound; similarly is the matter of the stars. If it were as he says, it would be thus by the planning of a wise knowing one who established them upon that. And if planning belonged to them, they would not be able to tire themselves with perpetual motion and movement and cause themselves pain; for such is the condition of living beings in the witnessed world: those states tire and pain them. Or if they were inanimate, then they would be under the planning of another, as occurred in the story of the brocade. Then, if it were permissible to say concerning our world that it is under the planning of someone mentioned, then it would be permissible similarly concerning someone mentioned that he was under the planning of one above him, and so on ad infinitum. In that is the invalidation of their claim about the planning of the stars; or it terminates in an end, and in that is the corruption of their claim of removing the end from things and necessitating the assertion of a single one to whom the planning of all that was mentioned returns.

Do you live as if you truly believe that God alone is the ultimate planner of every detail of your life, or do you sometimes feel anxious as if things are left to chance? How can you align your heart with this truth?

The Absurdity of Materialist Force on Matter
Maturidi ridicules the materialist's self-contradiction and exposes the faulty logic of force acting on matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the materialist claim that an unguided force can transform matter into the world.

Core Idea
Blind force without wisdom cannot produce order.

Maturidi begins his refutation by pointing out the logical inconsistencies in the materialist position. He attacks the philosopher who claims to have discovered this principle without being able to justify his own reasoning. Then he shows that if force can transform matter, it must either be independent of matter or not, leading to absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Focus on Maturidi's critique of the philosopher: 'the sick one' who has no wisdom. Notice how he questions the philosopher's authority.
2
Analyze the force and hyle argument
Examine the logical dilemma: if force can transform matter, it must have authority over other things. Maturidi uses this to redirect the argument to God.
3
Understand the conclusion
The existence of the world itself disproves the materialist principle, because constant change requires an external cause.
This conclusion sets up the positive argument in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السقيمة التي لا حكمة فيها ولا علم لديها؛ وهو أحد أبنائها الذي لم ينل شيئًا إلا بها. فمن أين قدم نفسه عليها؟ وإذا جاز ذلك، من غير أصل له به صار كذلك، فليقل في جميع العالم بمثل الذي قال بنفسه. ثم لا يخلو القوة التي هي قلبت الهيولى من أن يكون لها سلطان على "غيرها" بما به قلبتها؛ فليقل هو في الله سبحانه: أنشأ الهيولى أو ما شاء على وجه يقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب، ثم ليُسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبه. فإذا بطل الأصل الذي به العالم وهلك؛ الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلاكه انقلاب غير وقيامه. مع ما يكون في الهيولى، فتصير هي بلا قوة، التقليب فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما. فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما في الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث يصلح لشيء لم يكن يصلح له إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك. فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض [منه] كان كذلك كل على جعله كذلك.
The sick one who has no wisdom nor knowledge; and he is one of its sons who attained nothing except through it. So from where did he put himself forward over it? And if that is permissible, without any basis by which he became so, then let him say about the entire world the like of what he said about himself. Then the force that turned over the hyle (al-hyuli) cannot be without having authority over 'other than itself' by that by which it turned it over; so let him say about God, exalted: He originated the hyle or whatever He willed in a manner that accepts turning over and by which composition subsists, then let him name it whatever he wills regarding the annihilation of what He turned over. So when the principle by which the world exists is invalidated and perishes; it is impossible that the self-subsistent perishes so that by its perishing there is an overturning of another and its subsistence. Along with what is in the hyle, so it becomes without force, the overturning, so in that there is the invalidation of the world and its constant change from state to state. So its existence indicates the corruption of this principle. Along with what is observed: there is nothing that becomes suitable for something for which it was not suitable except through a wise maker who makes it so. So it is established that the beginning of the world, if it is possible that these substances and accidents [from it] exist, then it is so, all of it, upon His making it so.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage refutes the materialist principle that the world originated through a blind force (quwwa) acting on matter (hyuli) without a wise creator. The argument proceeds in several steps. First, Maturidi criticizes the philosopher who claims this principle but cannot justify his own ability to reason about it. He then argues that if force can transform matter, then one should attribute the origin of all things directly to God, who created matter and composition. The materialist principle leads to absurdities: if the force is inherent in matter, it cannot be separated; if it is not, the world's constant change requires an external cause. The existence of the world itself disproves this principle, because in the observable world (al-shahid), nothing becomes fit for a purpose except through a wise maker. Thus, the origin of the world, including all substances and accidents, is solely from God's making.

Key Terms
قوة (quwwa)
هيولى (hyuli)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi is attacking all philosophy and rational inquiry.
Correction: He is specifically refuting the materialist principle that blind force alone can create order, not all philosophy.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the existence of the world indicate?
A) That the materialist principle is false.
B) That the world is eternal.
C) That force is separate from matter.
D) That the philosopher is wise.

Key Takeaway
The materialist principle that blind force transforms matter is self-refuting and contradicted by the world's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You routinely attribute the order in your life—your health, your routine, your successes—to 'just how things work' or 'luck.' Are you not then like the materialist who puts himself forward over the very power that sustains him? Will you today consciously say, 'This is from Allah's wisdom,' even for the small things?
?
The materialist claims blind force can produce order. Do you ever secretly think that your own achievements are due to your cleverness rather than Allah's decree? What would change if you fully acknowledged that every ability and outcome is from Him? Write down one area where you need to repent of this mindset.
?
Maturidi exposes a contradiction in the materialist's worldview. When you examine your own beliefs, are there contradictions you ignore? For instance, do you ask Allah for help while also believing things happen by mere chance? How will you resolve this inconsistency starting today?

The Argument from Purpose for a Wise Creator
Maturidi uses the argument from purpose in the observable world to establish the necessity of a wise creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that observable things only become fit for their purposes through a wise maker, proving the need for a wise creator of the world.

Core Idea
Purpose in the world demands a wise maker.

After refuting the materialist principle, Maturidi presents a positive argument from observation. He states that in the observable world, nothing becomes suitable for something for which it was not suitable except through a wise maker who makes it so. This leads to the conclusion that the entire world, including all substances and accidents, is the result of God's making.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Notice the key phrase: 'along with what is observed' (مع ما في الشاهد). This introduces an empirical argument.
2
Understand the principle
The principle: nothing becomes suitable for a purpose it was not previously suitable for except through a wise maker. Think of examples like a key fitting a lock or an eye seeing.
3
Apply to the world's origin
The world as a whole, with its numerous purposes, must have been made by a wise maker. Thus, the origin of the world is from God's making.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السقيمة التي لا حكمة فيها ولا علم لديها؛ وهو أحد أبنائها الذي لم ينل شيئًا إلا بها. فمن أين قدم نفسه عليها؟ وإذا جاز ذلك، من غير أصل له به صار كذلك، فليقل في جميع العالم بمثل الذي قال بنفسه. ثم لا يخلو القوة التي هي قلبت الهيولى من أن يكون لها سلطان على "غيرها" بما به قلبتها؛ فليقل هو في الله سبحانه: أنشأ الهيولى أو ما شاء على وجه يقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب، ثم ليُسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبه. فإذا بطل الأصل الذي به العالم وهلك؛ الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلاكه انقلاب غير وقيامه. مع ما يكون في الهيولى، فتصير هي بلا قوة، التقليب فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما. فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما في الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث يصلح لشيء لم يكن يصلح له إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك. فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض [منه] كان كذلك كل على جعله كذلك.
The sick one who has no wisdom nor knowledge; and he is one of its sons who attained nothing except through it. So from where did he put himself forward over it? And if that is permissible, without any basis by which he became so, then let him say about the entire world the like of what he said about himself. Then the force that turned over the hyle (al-hyuli) cannot be without having authority over 'other than itself' by that by which it turned it over; so let him say about God, exalted: He originated the hyle or whatever He willed in a manner that accepts turning over and by which composition subsists, then let him name it whatever he wills regarding the annihilation of what He turned over. So when the principle by which the world exists is invalidated and perishes; it is impossible that the self-subsistent perishes so that by its perishing there is an overturning of another and its subsistence. Along with what is in the hyle, so it becomes without force, the overturning, so in that there is the invalidation of the world and its constant change from state to state. So its existence indicates the corruption of this principle. Along with what is observed: there is nothing that becomes suitable for something for which it was not suitable except through a wise maker who makes it so. So it is established that the beginning of the world, if it is possible that these substances and accidents [from it] exist, then it is so, all of it, upon His making it so.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage refutes the materialist principle that the world originated through a blind force (quwwa) acting on matter (hyuli) without a wise creator. The argument proceeds in several steps. First, Maturidi criticizes the philosopher who claims this principle but cannot justify his own ability to reason about it. He then argues that if force can transform matter, then one should attribute the origin of all things directly to God, who created matter and composition. The materialist principle leads to absurdities: if the force is inherent in matter, it cannot be separated; if it is not, the world's constant change requires an external cause. The existence of the world itself disproves this principle, because in the observable world (al-shahid), nothing becomes fit for a purpose except through a wise maker. Thus, the origin of the world, including all substances and accidents, is solely from God's making.

Key Terms
حكيم (hakim)
شاهد (shahid)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This is merely an argument from analogy, not a logical necessity.
Correction: Maturidi presents it as a universal observation (omneity) that is logically necessary: no object can self-attribute a new purpose without an external maker.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the only way something becomes suitable for a purpose it was not suitable for?
A) Through chance.
B) Through a wise maker.
C) Through its own nature.
D) Through time.

Key Takeaway
The observable fact that things acquire suitability only through a wise maker proves that the world's origin requires a wise creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you recognized that something in your life—a skill, a relationship, an opportunity—became suitable for a purpose you could not have achieved on your own. Did you credit a wise Maker, or did you assume it was just coincidence? What is at stake in your answer?
?
If every instance of suitability in your daily experience points to a wise Maker, then what does the existence of your own body—its complex systems and purposes—say about your relationship to the One who made it so? Are you living as if you are a product of random chance or of deliberate wisdom?
?
The argument establishes that the very beginning of the world is entirely dependent on God's making. If that is true, then your own existence at this moment is also dependent on His continuous act of making. Does your heart feel that dependence, or do you live as if you are self-sufficient? How might you remind yourself daily that you are 'upon His making it so'?

The Principle of Change Requires a Wise Changer
Maturidi states the principle of change requiring a changer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's foundational principle that every natural change requires an external changer, and that the soundness of consequences reveals a wise agent.

Core Idea
Every change in nature reveals its cause in its consequences.

Maturidi begins by establishing a foundational principle: anything with a nature (tab') cannot change without an external changer. He then shows that the outcome of the change distinguishes a wise changer from a foolish one. This refutes materialist theories of spontaneous change through mixture or motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation to understand the argument.
Notice the structure: first a methodological point, then a key principle, then its application.
2
Identify the two sources of knowledge
Maturidi says we can rely on revelation or infer from the present to the absent. Focus on the second method for this lesson.
3
Grasp the key principle
The principle: everything with a nature (tab') does not change except by a changer, either wise or foolish. The consequences (al-'awaqib) show which one.
This is the core of the argument.
4
See how it refutes materialists
Maturidi applies this to refute claims that the world originated from mixture, motion, or the turning of power. Such changes require a wise changer, not blind forces.
5
Reflect on the outcome
The passage establishes that the world's composition implies a wise originator. Think about why consequences are a reliable indicator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: والأصل في هذا عندنا وفيما ذكر من النجوم والطبائع أن لا يخلو من أن يرجع في ذلك إلى سمع - وفيها سماع أهل التوحيد أثبت، لما معهم براهين الصدق - أو يستدل بالحاضر الموجود على الغائب. فإن كان هذا طريقه فيجب - إذ الموجود على حال وبالوجود اعتباره - أن يكون الذي به وجد بهذه الصفة؛ فيبطل قولهم في حدوث العالم بالامتزاج وبتحرك النجوم، وتقليب القوة الهيولى؛ والهيولى والقوة جميعا؛ وإن كان على اعتبار معان في الموجود تدل عليه؛ فإن الأصل أن كل ذي طبع لا يتغير عما عليه إلى خلاف إلا بمغيّر حكيم أو سفيه، لكن يظهر أمرهما بالعواقب. فمثله الأصل الذي أشاروا إليه الأمر، إنه لا يصير على غير تلك الحال مما تصلح عواقبه إلا بحكيم؛ إذ هي كذلك. وذلك يبطل أصلهم ويثبت أن الأصل احتمل ما احتمل بجعله غيره كذلك، وفي ذلك حدثه بمحدث حكيم. وبالله التوفيق.

وأيضاً إن المعلوم فيما كان طبعه الإحراق أنه لا يحرق إلا المطبوع لاحتمال الاحتراق، وكذا التسويد وكل حال وجوهر. ثم ليس في طبع المحتمل الرفع إلى القابل فيه بالطبع، ولا في طبع المحرق أن يصير إلى من يحتمل ذلك. ومن أراد في الشاهد ذلك لا يتهيأ له دون العلم بالوجود والجمع بينهما، فعلى ذلك أمر ذلك الغائب. فيبطل الذي راموا إثباته ويصير هو بمعنى ما هم فيه. والله الموفق.

مع ما إذا كان جميع تلك الأصول التي قالوها هي مواتا لا تدبير لهن، ويعملن بالطبع لا اختيار لهن لم يجز أن يكون فيها منها وجود به يجيء عالما سميعا بصيرا قادرا حيا ميتا، وأن يكون محتملا لجهات ذلك خارجا من احتمال ذلك؛ ثبت كون ذلك كله بالمكون العليم. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The principle in this according to us and regarding what was mentioned of the stars and natures is that it cannot be free from either referring in that to revelation – and in it the hearing of the people of tawhid is more established, because they have proofs of truthfulness – or inferring from the present existent to the absent. If this is the way, then it is necessary – since the existent is in a state and by existence its consideration – that that by which it exists is with this attribute; thus their statement regarding the origination of the world by mixture, motion of stars, and the turning of the power of matter become invalid; and matter and power together; and if it were based on considering meanings in the existent that indicate it; then the principle is that everything with a nature does not change from what it is to its opposite except by a wise or foolish changer, but their outcome appears in consequences. So similarly the principle they pointed to is the matter, that it does not become upon other than that state from which its consequences are sound except by a wise [changer]; for it is like that. And that invalidates their principle and establishes that the principle contains what it contains by making another like that, and in that is its origination by a wise originator. And with Allah is success.

And also, the known regarding that whose nature is burning is that it does not burn except what is naturally prepared for the possibility of burning, and likewise blackening and every state and substance. Then it is not in the nature of that which is possible to be raised up to that which is receptive in it by nature, nor is it in the nature of the burner to become to the one who can receive that. And whoever aims for that in the witnessed cannot achieve it without knowledge of existence and combining them, so likewise is the affair of that absent. So what they aimed to establish is invalidated and becomes as he is in what they are. And Allah is the grantor of success.

Moreover, when all those principles which they said are lifeless, having no management, and they work by nature, having no choice, it is not possible that there would be from them an existence by which comes a knowing, hearing, seeing, powerful, living, dead being, and that it be capable of aspects of that outside of its capability; thus it is established that all that is by the knowing Maker. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof for the existence of a wise creator. Maturidi begins by stating that the principle regarding stars and natures must be based either on revelation (which is more established because it comes with proofs) or on inference from the present to the absent. If we use inference, since the existent world is in a certain state, its cause must have that attribute. This refutes the materialist claim that the world originated from mixture, motion, and the turning of power. The key principle is: everything with a nature (tab') does not change to its opposite except by a changer who is either wise or foolish, but the outcome (consequences) reveals which. Thus, anything that changes to a state with sound consequences requires a wise changer. This invalidates the materialist principle and shows that the world's composition implies a wise originator.

He then adds an analogy: what has a nature of burning only burns what is naturally receptive to burning; similarly, the receptive thing cannot raise itself to the burner by nature. In the witnessed world, achieving such an effect requires knowledge and combination, so the same applies to the unseen. Thus their position is invalidated.

Finally, he argues that since the material principles are lifeless and act by nature without choice, they cannot produce a being with attributes like knowledge, hearing, sight, power, life, and death. Therefore, all of this must come from the Knowing Maker (al-mukawwin al-'alim).

Key Terms
طبع (nature)
مغيّر حكيم (wise changer)
عواقب (consequences)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Natural changes can occur spontaneously without an external agent.
Correction: Maturidi argues that every change in a natural thing requires an external changer, and the soundness of consequences proves it is a wise agent.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what distinguishes a wise changer from a foolish one?
A) The duration of the change
B) The speed of the change
C) The consequences of the change
D) The location of the change

Key Takeaway
Every natural change requires an external changer, and sound consequences indicate a wise creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe changes in your own character or circumstances, do you instinctively trace them back to a wise Changer, or do you credit chance or your own efforts? What would it look like to live each day acknowledging Allah as that wise Changer behind every good outcome?
?
The passage says consequences reveal whether a changer is wise or foolish. Think of a recent change in your life whose outcome was clearly good. Did you thank the One who brought it about, or did you silently assume you deserved it? What does your response say about the state of your heart toward Allah?
?
Maturidi argues that nothing with a nature changes without an external agent. How does this truth expose your tendency to think you can change your own heart independently of Allah? What is one specific area of your life where you have been trying to change yourself without turning to Him, and what would it mean to surrender that change to the wise Changer today?

Arguments from Burning and Lifelessness
Maturidi presents two more proofs: from burning and from lifeless principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's additional arguments: the analogy of burning shows the need for a combining agent, and lifeless principles cannot produce living attributes.

Core Idea
Lifeless nature cannot generate life or consciousness without a knowing Maker.

Maturidi continues his proof with two further arguments. First, using the example of fire and combustible material, he shows that the effect requires a combination that nature alone cannot achieve. Second, he argues that the material principles (which are lifeless and act by nature without choice) cannot produce a being with attributes like knowledge, hearing, and sight. Therefore, all creation must come from the Knowing Maker.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the two distinct arguments separated by a paragraph break.
2
Analyze the burning analogy
Maturidi notes that fire (whose nature is burning) only burns what is naturally receptive. Neither the fire nor the combustible can bring about the burning by itself; it requires an agent who knows and combines them.
This shows the need for a wise agent beyond mere natures.
3
Understand the lifelessness argument
Maturidi argues that the material principles (stars, natures, matter) are lifeless (موات) and act by nature without choice. They cannot produce a being with life, knowledge, power, etc. So such attributes must come from a Knowing Maker.
This is a direct proof for a creator with knowledge.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Both arguments reinforce that natural causes are insufficient; a wise, knowing agent is necessary.

?

The Principle of Change Requires a Wise Changer
Maturidi states the principle that every natural change requires a changer, and uses the world's order to prove a wise Maker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why every natural change requires a wise or foolish changer, and how the outcome reveals the changer's nature.

Core Idea
Every natural change points to a wise or foolish agent behind it.

Maturidi begins his proof for a wise Creator by stating a universal principle: nothing in nature changes from its state to its opposite without a changer. The agent may be wise or foolish, but the outcome of the change—whether it leads to orderly results—reveals which one it is. This principle, he argues, applies to the entire cosmos, showing that its orderly operation must come from a wise Maker.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the principle
Read the Arabic passage once. Look for the statement about 'every natural thing' and its condition for change.
Notice that the author mentions both wise and foolish changers, but the outcome distinguishes them.
2
Understand how the principle applies to the world
The author says that if we consider the world's outcomes—its orderly, beneficial results—they indicate a wise changer, not a foolish one.
3
See how this refutes the opponents
The author concludes that this invalidates the opponents' principle that nature alone suffices. The fact that the world is orderly proves an intelligent agent.
This is a key move in kalam cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العالم بالامتزاج وبتحرك النجوم، وتقليب القوة الهيولى ؛ والهيولى والقوة جميعا؛ وإن كان كان على اعتبار معان في الموجود تدل عليه ؛ فإن الأصل أن كل ذي طبع لا يتغير عما عليه إلى خلاف إلا بمغيّر حكيم أو سفيه، لكن يظهر أمرهما بالعواقب فمثله الأصل الذي أشاروا إليه الأمر، إنه لا يصير على غير تلك الحال مما تصلح عواقبه إلا بحكيم؛ إذ هي كذلك. وذلك يبطل أصلهم ويثبت أن الأصل احتمل ما احتمل بجعله غيره كذلك، وفي ذلك حدثه بمحدث حكيم. وبالله التوفيق.

وأيضاً إن المعلوم فيما كان طبعه الإحراق أنه لا يحرق إلا المطبوع لاحتمال الاحتراق، وكذا التسويد وكل حال وجوهر . ثم ليس في طبع المحتمل الرفع إلى القابل فيه بالطبع، ولا في طبع المحرق أن يصير إلى من يحتمل ذلك. ومن أراد في الشاهد ذلك لا يتهيأ له دون العلم بالوجود والجمع بينهما، فعلى ذلك أمر ذلك الغائب. فيبطل الذي راموا إثباته ويصير هو بمعنى ما هم فيه. والله الموفق.

مع ما إذا كان جميع تلك الأصول التي قالوها هي موات لا تدبير لهن، ويعملن بالطبع لا اختيار لهن لم يجز أن يكون فيها منها وجود به يجيئ عالماً سميعا بصيرا قادرًا حيا ميتا، وأن يكون محتملاً لجهات ذلك خارجا من احتمال ذلك؛ ثبت كون ذلك كله بالمكون العليم. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
By mixture, and by the movement of stars, and the turning of the power of hyle; and hyle and power together; and if it were based on considering meanings in the existent that indicate Him—for the principle is that every natural thing does not change from its state to its opposite except by a wise or foolish changer, but their outcomes show their nature. So likewise the principle they referred to: that it does not become other than that state whose outcomes are sound except by a wise [agent]—since they are such. And that invalidates their principle and proves that the principle (i.e., the natural thing) underwent what it underwent by making it other than such, and in that is its origination by a wise originator. And with Allah is success.

Also, it is known that what is by nature burning does not burn except what is naturally disposed to combustion, similarly blackening, and every state and substance. Then it is not in the nature of the disposed to raise to the receptive in it by nature, nor in the nature of the burner to become one who is disposed to that. And whoever intends that in the witnessed (world) cannot achieve it without knowledge of existence and bringing them together; so likewise is the matter of that unseen (world). Thus what they sought to prove is invalid, and it becomes in the sense of what they are in. And Allah is the granter of success.

Moreover, since all those principles they stated are lifeless, having no governance, and act by nature without choice, it is not possible that from them there should come into existence a being that is knowing, hearing, seeing, powerful, living, dying, and that it should be capable of aspects of that exceeding its capacity; thus it is established that all of that is by the all-knowing Maker. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a two-part proof for the existence of a wise Creator, likely directed against materialist or dualist views that explain change by natural processes alone. The first part (from 'العالم بالامتزاج' to 'وبالله التوفيق') establishes a general principle: any natured thing (ذي طبع) cannot change from its state to its opposite except by a changer who is either wise (حكيم) or foolish (سفيه). The outcome of the change reveals which kind of changer it is—wise changes lead to good outcomes, foolish ones to bad. The author argues that since the outcome of the world's changes is orderly and good, it must be from a wise changer, thus invalidating the opponents' claim that nature alone can produce such order.

The second part (from 'وأيضاً' to 'والله الموفق') uses the example of fire and burning to illustrate a deeper point: a naturally burning thing only burns what is naturally disposed to combustion; it cannot by itself generate the disposition to be burned in a thing that is not so disposed. In the physical world, achieving such a combination requires knowledge and intention. Therefore, the unseen world (الغائب) must also involve a knowing agent, ruling out the idea that nature alone accounts for the correspondence between causes and effects.

The final paragraph (from 'مع ما إذا كان' to the end) concludes that all the 'principles' (الأصول) the opponents posit—such as atoms, natures, or elements—are lifeless (موات) and act without intelligence. It is impossible for such dead, non-intelligent entities to produce a living, knowing, powerful being like a human. Therefore, the entire universe must depend on the all-knowing Maker (المكون العليم).

Throughout, the author follows the order of argument: first a general principle about change, then a specific example (fire), then a concluding argument from the impossibility of lifeless matter producing intelligent beings.

Key Terms
الهيولى
الطبع
الحكيم
السفيه
المحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think natural changes are self-sufficient and need no external cause.
Correction: Maturidi shows that every change requires a changer, and the order in the world proves that changer is wise.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the outcome of a natural change reveal?
A) Whether the changer is wise or foolish
B) The material composition of the thing
C) Whether the change is necessary
D) The time of day

Key Takeaway
Every natural change requires a changer, and the orderly world points to a wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument says that the outcomes of changes reveal the nature of the changer. Look at a major decision you made recently—what were its outcomes? What do those outcomes say about the wisdom of the one who made the choice? Will you commit to consulting the Wise Changer before your next big decision?
?
If every change in your life requires a changer, and the orderly outcomes point to a wise Creator, then what does your disorderly behavior (e.g., a recurring sin or bad habit) say about your own wisdom? Are you acting as a wise agent or a foolish one? How will you change your changer today?
?
The passage contrasts a wise changer who produces sound outcomes with a foolish one who produces unsound. Consider a time you blamed Allah for an apparent chaos in your life. Could it be that the chaos came from your own foolishness or a lack of trust in the Wise Changer? How can you align your will with His wisdom starting now?

The Example of Fire Shows the Need for a Knowing Agent
Maturidi uses the example of fire to show that natural causation needs a knowing agent to establish the cause-effect correspondence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why natural causes like fire cannot act on anything without a preexisting disposition, which requires a knowing designer.

Core Idea
Fire cannot burn what is not naturally disposed to burn—the match between cause and effect implies a wise designer.

Maturidi offers a powerful analogy from common experience: fire only burns materials that are naturally combustible. It cannot by itself create the capacity to be burned in something that lacks it. In the physical world, making such a correspondence work requires knowledge and will. Maturidi argues that the same holds in the unseen realm of divine action, refuting the idea that nature alone can account for the regularities we observe.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about fire and burning
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the distinction between what is naturally burning and what is naturally disposed to be burned.
The passage says: 'لا يحرق إلا المطبوع لاحتمال الاحتراق'.
2
Understand the logical gap
The author points out that it is not in the nature of the disposed to spontaneously acquire the capacity to be burned, nor is it in the nature of the burner to become disposed. Something else must bring them together.
3
Apply to the unseen
Just as in the witnessed world this combination requires knowledge and existence, so in the unseen it requires a knowing agent.
This is an argument from analogical reasoning (qiyās al-ghā'ib 'alā al-shāhid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

intermediate

Lifeless Principles Cannot Produce Intelligent Beings
Maturidi argues that lifeless, non-intelligent principles cannot produce intelligent beings, concluding for the all-knowing Maker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the universe cannot be explained by mindless principles alone, and must depend on an all-knowing Maker.

Core Idea
Dead, mindless elements cannot produce a living, intelligent being.

Maturidi concludes his proof by considering the ultimate failure of materialist explanations. The 'principles' that materialists invoke—like atoms, natures, or elements—are lifeless and act without choice. It is impossible for such things to give rise to a being that knows, hears, sees, has power, and lives. This final argument decisively shows that the entire cosmos depends on a Maker who is fully knowing and wise.

Guided Path
1
Read the final passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the description of the opponents' principles as 'lifeless' (موات) and acting 'by nature' (بالطبع) without choice.
2
Understand the impossibility argument
The author argues that from lifeless, non-intelligent bases, you cannot get a being that has attributes like knowledge, life, power, etc. This is a causal mismatch.
This resembles the 'from nothing, nothing comes' argument.
3
See the conclusion
The only valid conclusion is that all of existence is made by the all-knowing Maker (المكون العليم).
The phrase 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' is a closing praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?

The Samaniyya Claim and al-Nazzam's Refutation
The Samaniyya claim and al-Nazzam's counter-arguments, with Maturidi's dismissive comment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Samaniyya's argument for the earth's perpetual fall and how al-Nazzam attempted to refute it, as well as Maturidi's critique of that debate.

Core Idea
A flawed argument can still reveal the need for a deeper proof.

The Samaniyya sect held that the earth is constantly falling due to its weight. Al-Nazzam countered with colorful analogies, but Maturidi found the debate insufficient. This lesson explores that exchange and its limitations, setting the stage for a more robust proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Samaniyya claim
Read the passage to find what the Samaniyya believed about the earth's motion. Note their reasoning: the earth is heavy and therefore falls.
They agreed with others on temporal origination but differed on this point.
2
Examine al-Nazzam's first counter
Al-Nazzam uses the example of a stone and a feather to show that weight affects speed, yet the earth is heaviest and still doesn't fall faster. Understand this analogy.
This is a reductio ad absurdum from their own premise.
3
Examine al-Nazzam's second counter
He refers to the wind lifting objects upward to question why the earth cannot be lifted from below. Consider the logic.
4
Reflect on the conclusion of the debate
Al-Nazzam cuts off the discussion, implying he has made his point. But Maturidi remarks that the debate is like play. Why?
5
Grasp Maturidi's critique
Maturidi suggests the debate lacks substance and does not reach the real issue. Think about what a proper argument would require.
This transitions to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
أقاويل السمنية وبيان فسادها

وقالت السمنية من الدهرية، مع موافقتهم في حدوث الأشياء في الأزل: إن الأرض لا تزال تهوى سفلاً بمن عليها. فسألهم عن ذلك النظام، فاحتجوا بثقلها، والثقيل لا يقاوم الهواء ولا يقوم في الجو. فعارضهم بسرعة انحدار الحجر بثقله إذا أُرسل مع الريشة، ثم كانت الأرض منهما أثقل، وقد أدركاها. ثم عارضهم بما رأوا الريح تحمل الشيء فتصعد به في العلو دون الجوانب. فما يدريكم لو كانت تحت الأرض فتحملها بقوتها ؟ فكيف حكمتم بأن يهوى [الشيء] دون أن يصعد ويرتفع، وقد رأيتم مثله؟» وقطع الكلام على هذا. وإذا كان ذا حاصل المناظرة فما أشبهها بالملاعبة. بل الأصل إذ كنا نعاين السماء منذ عايناها على حالة واحدة وعاينا الأرض على ثقلها، وعلى ما كان كل جزء من أجزائها لو أرسل من أعلى موضع يبلغه الوهم لكان يلحقها . دل أن الأرض إذ قرت على حال وكذلك السماء، وهما في طبيعتهما بطبع الثقل ، وأن لا قرار لهما في الهواء، ثبت أن قرارهما بقوى حكيم، وأنه منشئهما على ما لا يدركه الأوهام ولا يبلغه العقول. وفي ذلك بطلان الدهر وفروعه. ما كانت مناظرة هؤلاء عبثًا، إذ طريقها البحث عن الأمور الخفية لتنجلى، وعن مع الوقوف على حدود الحكمة. وهم جعلوا العالم على ما عليه من الاختلاف والاتفاق واختلاف الجواهر والأعراض قائمات بالطباع مولدات عن حركات أشياء، أو مشوبات بما لا تدبير لها ولا علم ولا على حكمةٍ تَقْدِر، ويكون البشر أحد هؤلاء، فمحال أن يكون عندهم علم
Section (Mas'ala)
The sayings of the Samaniyya and demonstration of their corruption.

The Samaniyya of the Dahriyya said, while agreeing with them on the temporal origination of things in pre-eternity [azal], that the earth continually falls downward with whatever is upon it. Al-Nazzam asked them about that, and they argued by its weight: the heavy does not resist the air nor stand in the atmosphere. He countered them with the speed of descent of a stone by its weight when released with a feather, but the earth is heavier than both, and they have perceived it. Then he countered them with what they saw: the wind carries a thing and lifts it upwards rather than sideways. 'How do you know that if it were under the earth it would not carry it by its force? How did you judge that it falls downward without rising and ascending, when you have seen something like it?' And he cut off the discussion on this. If this is the outcome of the debate, how similar it is to play! Rather, the principle is: since we have observed the sky from the time we observed it in one state, and we have observed the earth in its heaviness, and that every part of its parts, if released from the highest place imagination can reach, would reach it (i.e., the earth), this indicates that when the earth settled in its state and likewise the sky, and both are by their nature in the nature of heaviness, and they have no stability in the air, it is established that their stability is by the power of a wise [being], and that He is their Originator in a way that imaginations do not perceive nor intellects reach. In that is the invalidation of dahriyya (eternalism) and its branches. The debate of these people was not in vain, for its method is investigation into hidden matters to be revealed, and into the understanding of the limits of wisdom. They made the world, as it is with its differences and agreements, and the differences of substances and accidents, subsisting by natures, generated from movements of things, or mixed with that which has no governance nor knowledge nor according to a wise power, and human beings are one of these. So it is impossible that they have knowledge.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Samaniyya (السمنية), a sect of the Dahriyya (مادية / دهريون) who believed in the eternity of the world but still held that things originate in time. They argued that the earth is perpetually falling downward due to its weight. Al-Nazzam (النظام), a well-known Mu'tazilite theologian, responded to them with two counter-arguments: first, if a stone and a feather are released, the stone falls faster, but the earth is heavier than both, so by their logic it should fall even faster—yet it does not; second, the wind lifts things upward, so they cannot assume that nothing could lift the earth from below. Al-Nazzam then dismisses the debate.

Maturidi comments that such debate is like play, and he offers his own positive argument: we observe that the sky and earth have remained fixed for as long as we can remember. Both are heavy by nature, and heavy things have no natural stability in the air. Therefore, their continued stability must be due to the power of a wise Being (قوى حكيم), who created them in a way beyond human imagination and intellect. This refutes the entire eternalist (الدهر) worldview.

Maturidi then criticizes the Samaniyya's overall method: they treat the world—with all its order, differences, substances and accidents—as subsisting by natures, generated from movements of things, or as mixed with entities that have no governance, knowledge, or wise power. If that were the case, and humans are part of this system, then they could have no real knowledge (since knowledge would be merely a product of blind nature). Thus their own position is self-refuting.

The passage moves from reporting the Samaniyya's claim and al-Nazzam's debate, to Maturidi's own demonstration from observation, to a final logical refutation that undermines the materialist epistemology.

Key Terms
السمنية
الدهرية
النظام
الثقل
الهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that al-Nazzam's debate provides a sufficient refutation of the Samaniyya's claim.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly says the debate is like play, implying that it does not constitute a proper theological refutation.

Checkpoint
What is the Samaniyya's main argument for the earth falling?
A) The earth is heavy and heavy things have no stability in air.
B) The wind pushes the earth downward.
C) The sky is falling separately.
D) The earth is light and floats.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nazzam's counter-arguments expose flaws in the Samaniyya's reasoning, but Maturidi shows that such debate is superficial and a deeper proof is needed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there arguments you rely on for your faith that are as superficial as the Samaniyya's? What would it take for you to replace them with a deeper proof?
?
Al-Nazzam used clever analogies, but Maturidi saw them as play. When have you settled for a clever reason instead of seeking solid truth in your beliefs?
?
Do you treat theological discussions as a game of wit, or do you truly seek to know the Creator? How can you recognize the difference in your own heart?

Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
Maturidi's Proof from Stability and Refutation of Eternalism
Maturidi's own proof from the stability of the cosmos and his refutation of the materialist epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's own argument for a wise Creator based on the observed stability of the heavens and earth, and how this refutes the materialist worldview.

Core Idea
The stability of the heavy earth and sky points to a wise sustainer beyond natural forces.

After dismissing the earlier debate, Maturidi presents his own powerful proof: we see that the sky and earth remain fixed despite their natural heaviness. This cannot be explained by mere natures; it requires a wise Power. This argument not only proves God's existence but demolishes the entire eternalist framework.

Guided Path
1
Observe the stability
Read the passage and note Maturidi's observation: the sky and earth have been in the same state for as long as we can remember. This is the starting point.
2
Understand the natural condition
Both earth and sky are heavy by nature. Heavy things have no natural stability in the air; they should fall.
3
Draw the inference
Since they are stable despite their nature, their stability must come from an external power. Maturidi identifies this as the power of a wise being (حكيم).
4
See the refutation of eternalism
This conclusion invalidates the entire worldview of the Dahriyya (eternalists) and its branches.
5
Grasp the epistemological critique
Maturidi further argues that if the world were only natures, humans could not have knowledge, since knowledge requires a source beyond blind nature.

Source Text

Section (Mas'ala)
The sayings of the Samaniyya and demonstration of their corruption.

Al-Nazzam asked them about that, and they argued by its weight: the heavy does not resist the air nor stand in the atmosphere. He countered them with the speed of descent of a stone by its weight when released with a feather, but the earth is heavier than both, and they have perceived it. Then he countered them with what they saw: the wind carries a thing and lifts it upwards rather than sideways. 'How do you know that if it were under the earth it would not carry it by its force? How did you judge that it falls downward without rising and ascending, when you have seen something like it?' And he cut off the discussion on this. Rather, the principle is: since we have observed the sky from the time we observed it in one state, and we have observed the earth in its heaviness, and that every part of its parts, if released from the highest place imagination can reach, would reach it (i.e., the earth), this indicates that when the earth settled in its state and likewise the sky, and both are by their nature in the nature of heaviness, and they have no stability in the air, it is established that their stability is by the power of a wise [being], and that He is their Originator in a way that imaginations do not perceive nor intellects reach. So it is impossible that they have knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence Maturidi uses to prove the existence of a wise being?
A) The earth is too heavy to be held by air.
B) The sky and earth have remained stable despite their natural heaviness.
C) The wind can lift things, proving a hidden force.
D) The Samaniyya have no knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's argument from the stability of the heavens and earth provides a robust proof for a wise Creator and refutes the materialist worldview.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the sky and the earth, do you see them as signs of a wise Creator's constant maintenance, or do you walk through your day as if their stability is automatic? What would change if you consciously attributed every moment of stability to Allah's power?
?
The materialist worldview reduces humans to mere products of blind nature. Have you ever caught yourself living as if your choices, intellect, and purpose are ultimately meaningless—just chemicals and movements? How does Maturidi's refutation compel you to reclaim the truth of your divine origin and accountability?
?
If, as Maturidi argues, true knowledge is impossible without recognizing the wise Creator, then how often do you seek knowledge without first acknowledging that all wisdom comes from Him? What is one way you can begin each study with a conscious turn to Allah?

The Regress of Principles in Dualism
Maturidi enumerates a regress from two to four to six to seven or five principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses infinite regress to show the absurdity of the dualist claim that two eternal principles explain the world.

Core Idea
If two principles explain mixture, consistency demands four, six, seven—an endless chain.

Imam Maturidi begins his refutation of dualism by pushing their logic to its extreme. If opposition requires two principles, then why not four for the four natures, or six for the directions, or seven for their bearer? He shows that the dualists cannot stop at two without being arbitrary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the sequence of numbers: 2, 4, 6, 7, 5.
The passage builds a logical chain from the dualist's own premise.
2
Identify each step in the regress
List the principles Maturidi mentions: two (dualist claim), then four (natures), then six (directions), then seven (bearer) or five (composite).
3
Understand the reasoning behind each step
For each step, ask: what is the principle that forces the next number? Why does Maturidi say 'it would be necessary'?
The key is that the dualists' own method of positing principles for opposites leads to more opposites.
4
Reflect on the absurdity
Consider why the regress is a problem: if dualists can stop at two arbitrarily, their system lacks logical consistency.
This exposes dualism as a human construct, not a rational necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن الخير كله لكل من ذلك، فصيّروا النور خارجا عن أعظم الخير، والآخر عن أعظم الشر، ثم حققوا الأمرين لواحد وله قالوا بالاثنين. ليُعلم هلاك كل فريق بالذي به ظن النجاة. وبالله التوفيق. مع ما لو كان لذينك الوجهين يجب القول بالاثنين ليجب القول بالأربع نحو الطبائع، إذ هي متضادة، كل يضر الكل. ولو كان بهذا القول بالأربع ليجب القول بالست، بما لا يخلو شيء قائم عن جهات ست؛ وذلك يوجب القول بالسابع، لما كان حامل تلك الجهات لا يوصف بجهة سابقها؛ أو بالخمس بما كان الذي فيه اجتماع تلك الطبائع هو الخامس، وهو لا يوصف بحرّ ولا بَرْد. ولو كان كما تقول الثنوية ليجب القول بالثالث، لما كانا ولم يكن العالم ولا خير ولا شر. ومحال كون متبائن بنفسه ممتزجا بنفسه وهو لا يوجب الاجتماع والتناقض؛ ثبت كون ذلك بغيرهما، وبه كان كل خير وشر. فيبطل قولهم من حيث راموا إثباته.
All good is from each of that, so they made light outside of the greatest good, and the other [darkness] outside of the greatest evil. Then they confirmed the two matters to one, and they said by two. So that the destruction of every group might be known by that through which they thought salvation. And with Allah is success. Moreover, if for those two aspects it is necessary to say two, then it would be necessary to say four, like the natures, for they are mutually opposed, each harming the whole. And if by this [one] says four, then it would be necessary to say six, because no existent thing is free from six directions; and that necessitates saying the seventh, since the bearer of those directions is not described by a direction prior to them; or saying the fifth, because that in which those natures are combined is the fifth, and it is described neither by heat nor cold. And if it were as the dualists say, then it would be necessary to say the third, since there were the two, and there was no world, nor good, nor evil. And it is impossible for two things distinct in themselves to be mixed by themselves, [and] that does not necessitate union and contradiction; it is established that that [union] is by another than them, and by Him every good and evil exists. Thus their statement is invalidated from where they sought to prove it.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation of dualism (the belief in two eternal principles, light and darkness). Imam Maturidi begins by noting that the dualists made light separate from the greatest good and darkness separate from the greatest evil, and then they posited two principles for one reality. He then argues that if one accepts that two opposing principles are required to explain mixture, consistency would demand accepting four principles (like the four primary qualities: heat, cold, wetness, dryness) because these are also mutually opposed. But then one would need six for directions, and then a seventh for the bearer of directions, or a fifth for the substrate of the four qualities. This shows the arbitrary nature of dualism. Furthermore, if one follows the dualist logic, a third principle would be necessary because before the world existed, there were only the two principles, and yet no world, good, or evil existed; the mixture itself requires an external agent. It is impossible for two inherently distinct entities to mix themselves without causing union and contradiction. Therefore, the mixture must be caused by another (God), and through Him both good and evil occur. Thus the dualist position is refuted by the very method they used to try to prove it.

Key Terms
الطبائع
الجهات الست

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism is refuted only by scripture or revelation.
Correction: Imam Maturidi refutes dualism by logical consistency: their own method leads to an infinite regress of principles.

Checkpoint
What is the first step in Maturidi's regress argument after the dualists' two principles?
A) Six directions
B) Four natures
C) Seven bearers
D) Five composites

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes dualism by showing that its own logic demands an endless chain of principles, making it absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience personal trials or see evil in the world, do you ever unconsciously imagine a force competing with God? How does Maturidi's logical argument expose that tendency as intellectually unstable, and what inner shift does it demand from you?
?
What would it mean for your daily reliance on God if you truly believed that no other power—no 'second principle'—can ultimately oppose His will? How might your prayers, fears, and decisions change starting tomorrow?
?
Have you ever accepted a comfortable compromise in your faith that diluted the absolute oneness of God—perhaps by attributing some power to habits, people, or fate? How does this argument call you to abandon such compromises and embrace a more consistent tawheed?

The Necessity of a Single Creator
Maturidi argues that mixture of opposites needs a third cause, refuting dualism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the mixture of opposites requires a single external cause, thereby establishing monotheism.

Core Idea
Two opposites cannot mix themselves; a third cause is necessary, and that is God.

After exposing the absurd regress, Maturidi delivers the decisive argument: the dualists cannot explain how light and darkness interact without a third principle. He proves that mixture requires an external agent, thus establishing the necessity of a single Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the logical condition: 'if it were as the dualists say, then it would be necessary to say the third.'
The passage moves from conditional to conclusion.
2
Understand the impossibility of self-mixture
Maturidi states it is impossible for two distinct things to mix by themselves. Ask: why is it impossible? Because they are opposite and cannot unite without a unifier.
3
Identify the external cause
The passage concludes that mixture must be by 'another than them,' and that this other is the source of all good and evil.
This other is the one Creator.
4
Reflect on the refutation
The dualists tried to prove their position, but their own logic leads to its invalidation. Note the phrase 'from where they sought to prove it.'
This is a powerful rhetorical and logical conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن الخير كله لكل من ذلك، فصيّروا النور خارجا عن أعظم الخير، والآخر عن أعظم الشر، ثم حققوا الأمرين لواحد وله قالوا بالاثنين. ليُعلم هلاك كل فريق بالذي به ظن النجاة. وبالله التوفيق. مع ما لو كان لذينك الوجهين يجب القول بالاثنين ليجب القول بالأربع نحو الطبائع، إذ هي متضادة، كل يضر الكل. ولو كان بهذا القول بالأربع ليجب القول بالست، بما لا يخلو شيء قائم عن جهات ست؛ وذلك يوجب القول بالسابع، لما كان حامل تلك الجهات لا يوصف بجهة سابقها؛ أو بالخمس بما كان الذي فيه اجتماع تلك الطبائع هو الخامس، وهو لا يوصف بحرّ ولا بَرْد. ولو كان كما تقول الثنوية ليجب القول بالثالث، لما كانا ولم يكن العالم ولا خير ولا شر. ومحال كون متبائن بنفسه ممتزجا بنفسه وهو لا يوجب الاجتماع والتناقض؛ ثبت كون ذلك بغيرهما، وبه كان كل خير وشر. فيبطل قولهم من حيث راموا إثباته.
All good is from each of that, so they made light outside of the greatest good, and the other [darkness] outside of the greatest evil. Then they confirmed the two matters to one, and they said by two. So that the destruction of every group might be known by that through which they thought salvation. And with Allah is success. Moreover, if for those two aspects it is necessary to say two, then it would be necessary to say four, like the natures, for they are mutually opposed, each harming the whole. And if by this [one] says four, then it would be necessary to say six, because no existent thing is free from six directions; and that necessitates saying the seventh, since the bearer of those directions is not described by a direction prior to them; or saying the fifth, because that in which those natures are combined is the fifth, and it is described neither by heat nor cold. And if it were as the dualists say, then it would be necessary to say the third, since there were the two, and there was no world, nor good, nor evil. And it is impossible for two things distinct in themselves to be mixed by themselves, [and] that does not necessitate union and contradiction; it is established that that [union] is by another than them, and by Him every good and evil exists. Thus their statement is invalidated from where they sought to prove it.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation of dualism (the belief in two eternal principles, light and darkness). Imam Maturidi begins by noting that the dualists made light separate from the greatest good and darkness separate from the greatest evil, and then they posited two principles for one reality. He then argues that if one accepts that two opposing principles are required to explain mixture, consistency would demand accepting four principles (like the four primary qualities: heat, cold, wetness, dryness) because these are also mutually opposed. But then one would need six for directions, and then a seventh for the bearer of directions, or a fifth for the substrate of the four qualities. This shows the arbitrary nature of dualism. Furthermore, if one follows the dualist logic, a third principle would be necessary because before the world existed, there were only the two principles, and yet no world, good, or evil existed; the mixture itself requires an external agent. It is impossible for two inherently distinct entities to mix themselves without causing union and contradiction. Therefore, the mixture must be caused by another (God), and through Him both good and evil occur. Thus the dualist position is refuted by the very method they used to try to prove it.

Key Terms
الثنوية
المتبائن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism can explain mixture by the inherent nature of opposites.
Correction: Maturidi shows that inherently distinct things cannot mix themselves; an external unifier is needed.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why must there be a third principle besides the two dualist principles?
A) Because the two principles are not eternal
B) Because the world existed before the two
C) Because the two alone did not produce the world, good, or evil
D) Because the two are actually the same

Key Takeaway
Dualism is refuted because it cannot account for the interaction of opposites without a single Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever silently doubted that God alone is the source of both good and evil, especially when faced with overwhelming hardship? How does this passage confront that doubt directly?
?
Do you live as though your ability to do good comes from yourself, or do you truly acknowledge that every good deed is from God alone? What would change if you internally affirmed this every moment?
?
If Maturidi’s argument is true, then to attribute any independent power to causes other than God is a form of hidden dualism. Where in your heart do you still see 'two sources' competing with God’s oneness, and what step will you take tonight to uproot that?

The Error of Anthropomorphism in Dualists
Maturidi critiques dualists for anthropomorphizing God and failing to grasp divine wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi identifies the dualists' error as stemming from intellectual limitation and anthropomorphism, and how this leads to a flawed understanding of divine unity.

Core Idea
Dualism is not an alternative but an error rooted in ignorance and measuring God by human standards.

Imam Maturidi now turns to a direct critique of dualist thought. He argues that the very claim that God must be composed of two principles (light and darkness) reveals a fundamental failure to grasp divine wisdom. Instead of acknowledging God's transcendence, the dualists project their own limitations onto the Creator. In this passage, Maturidi exposes the intellectual blind spot that leads to such a mistaken worldview.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the flow from a general statement about tawhid to a specific critique of dualists.
2
Identify the dualists' root error
Find where Maturidi explains why the dualists went wrong. Look for the phrase about their intellects not reaching the level of divine wisdom.
This is the core of the critique.
3
Understand their anthropomorphism
Notice how Maturidi says they thought the Lord would have human needs and vulnerabilities. This is a key form of anthropomorphism.
They are measuring God by themselves.
4
Reflect on the consequences
Consider what Maturidi says would happen if they reflected on their own limitations. What would they realize?
Ignorance blocks perception of wisdom.
5
Analyze the specific dualist claim
Focus on the final sentence where Maturidi mentions the mixture of light and darkness. Why does this self-contradict their claim to wisdom?
A pure principle cannot be mixed without impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول بالواحد لا يضطر صاحبه إلى القول بآخر بوجه وأصل ذلك أن هؤلاء قوم لم تبلغ عقولهم المبلغ الذي تدرك به حكمة الربوبية في الأشياء، وظنوا أن يكون الرب على صفتهم من الحاجات والشهوات واحتمال الآفات وشوائب العاهات، فقدروا فعله بالذي علموا الحكمة بأفعال أنفسهم. ولو تأملوا ما هم فيه من الضرورات السواتر المانعة عن الإحاطة بالأشياء، ثم بمصالح أنفسهم التي في ذلك جل كدهم، وجهدوا لعلموا أن الجهل هو الذي سدّهم عن إدراك الحكمة في ذلك. وأحق الناس بهذا هم؛ إذ زعموا أن العالم إنما امتزاج النور والظلمة، فما من جزء من أجزاء النور إلا هو مشوب بجزء من أجزاء الظلمة.
Then, the statement of the One does not compel its adherent to say another in any way. The origin of that is that these are a people whose intellects have not reached the level by which the wisdom of lordship in things is perceived. They thought that the Lord would be upon their description of needs, desires, susceptibility to afflictions, and blemishes of defects. So they estimated His act by that by which they knew wisdom from their own acts. If they had reflected upon what they are in of necessities veiling them from encompassing things, then upon the interests of their own selves which in that is the bulk of their exertion, they would have striven and known that ignorance is what blocked them from perceiving wisdom in that. And the most deserving of people with this are they, since they claimed that the world is only a mixture of light and darkness, and there is no part of the parts of light except it is mixed with a part of the parts of darkness.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage shifts to a direct critique of dualist methodology. Imam Maturidi states that affirming the oneness of God does not force one to posit a second principle. The root error of the dualists is that their intellects are too limited to grasp divine wisdom. They mistakenly attribute human needs, desires, and vulnerabilities to God, measuring His actions by their own. If they had considered the limitations and veils that prevent them from fully understanding things, and the difficulty of their own interests, they would realize that ignorance prevents them from comprehending wisdom. The dualists are especially guilty because they claim the world is a mixture of light and darkness, implying that every part of light is contaminated with darkness. This contradicts their claim to wisdom, as a pure principle (light) cannot be mixed without losing its purity.

الجهل

Correction: Maturidi shows that dualism originates from intellectual limitation and anthropomorphism, not sound reasoning.

A) Following scripture
B) Their intellects being too limited to grasp divine wisdom
C) Their rejection of prophets
D) Their preference for Greek philosophy

Key Takeaway
Dualism is not a valid alternative to tawhid; it is a product of intellectual limitation and anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
